TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
 
TB Resolution 2025-450 
 
AUTHORIZES DESIGNATED ALCOHOL SERVICE VENDORS TO SERVE 
ALCOHOL AT THE “MOSAIC COMMUNITY STREET PAINTING FESTIVAL” 
 
Councilman Kern offered the following resolution, 
which was seconded by Councilwoman Merrifield 
 
WHEREAS, the Riverhead Town Board approved a Chapter 255 special event 
permit for the East End Arts & Humanities Council by Resolutions No. 2025 -128 
adopted on January 22, 2025 and No. 2025 -412 adopted on May 6, 2025, to conduct 
the MOSAIC COMMUNITY STREET PAINTING FESTIVAL on Sunday, June 1, 2025 
(rain date Sunday, June 15, 2025 from 12:00 p.m. to 5:00 p.m., on Main Street and at 
133 East Main Street, Riverhead, New York, as outlined on the attached map (Schedule 
“A”); and 
 
WHEREAS, East End Arts & Humanities Council has requested permission to 
permit alcohol service from designated vendors within the licensed premises at the 
afore-mentioned location, dates and time; and 
 
WHEREAS, East End Arts & Humanities Counsel has designated the following 
alcohol service vendors regarding participation in the “Mosaic Community Street 
Painting Festival”: 
 
Northfork Brewing Co. 
24 East 2nd Street, Suite A 
Riverhead, NY 11901.  
 
Peconic Bay Vineyards 
31320 Main Rd 
Cutchogue, NY 11935 
 
NOW THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED , that the Town of Riverhead approves 
participation of the above -referenced alcohol service vendors regarding alcohol service 
at the “Mosaic Community Street Painting Festival at the afore -mentioned location, 
dates and time, subject to the following conditions: 
 
1. Each participating alcohol service vendor shall comply with New York State 
Alcohol Beverage Control Laws, NYS Liquor Authority Rules and 
Regulations, NYS Governor Executive Orders, including successive 
Orders, the Town of Riverhead Alcohol Policy and Town Code provisions, 
as applicable. 
 
2. Each participating alcohol service vendor shall execute a license 
agreement in a form to be approved by the Town Attorney’s Office. 
 
10.30
Packet Pg. 114
3. Each participating alcohol service vendor shall procure a general liability 
insurance policy for the subject activity naming the Town of Riverhead, 
Town of Riverhead Business Improvement District and Riverhead Business 
Improvement District Management Association, Inc., as “additional 
insureds” on a primary and non -contributory basis, with policy limits of at 
least $1,000,000 per occurrence/ $2,000,000 aggregate, including 
food/product service liability protection, if applicable.  In addition to the 
above referenced insurance requirements, alcohol service vendors shall 
also procure an additional insurance liability policy regarding alcohol 
service liability with policy limits of at least $2,000,000.00 dollars per 
occurrence/$2 million dollars aggregate which shall name the above -
referenced parties as additional insureds also on a primary and non -
contributory basis. 
 
4.  Alcohol service shall also be subject to the following conditions: 
 
a. All alcohol servers must be TIPS (Training for Intervention Procedures) 
approved by New York State. 
b. Alcohol service and consumption shall be limited to the authorized and 
approved alcohol service vendors as limited to the licensed premises 
addressed above (as delineated on the Mosaic Festival map). 
c. Alcohol service shall be solely limited to beer, cider, wine and/or 
champagne.   
d. Alcohol service shall be limited to two (2) drinks per age-appropriate -
customer at a time. 
e. Licensee shall possess and provide, prior to participation, a valid New 
York State Liquor Authority catering permit, or other appropriate permit, 
regarding off-premises alcohol service and comply with all applicable 
permit requirements including all other applicable municipal laws, rules 
and regulations, including service hours. 
f. Alcohol service shall be served in clear plastic cups and contain an 
identifying symbol and/or logo uniquely identifying the vendor. Each 
such cup shall be limited in size to 12 oz. for beer/cider; 5 oz. for 
wine/champagne. 
g. Alcohol servers shall be required to hand-stamp age-appropriate 
alcohol patrons prior to alcohol service. 
h. Such other conditions as may be more fully delineated in the alcohol 
vendor license agreement and Town alcohol policy; 
i. BIDMA shall retain a private security company at its own cost and 
expense to monitor alcohol consumption activity. 
 
 and be it further 
 
RESOLVED, that the Town of Riverhead waives the Town of Riverhead alcohol 
policy requirement regarding submission of a security/damage deposit by participating 
alcohol service vendors; and be it further 
 
RESOLVED, that the Town Supervisor is authorized to execute license 
agreements with participating alcohol service vendors in a form to be approved by the 
Town Attorney’s Office; and be it further  
 
10.30
Packet Pg. 115

resolution to Chief Ed Frost, Riverhead Town Police Department; Andrew Smith, Chief 
Fire Marshal, the Engineering Department and the Town Attorney’s Office; and be it 
further  
 
RESOLVED, that all Town Hall Departments may review and obtain a copy of 
this resolution from the electronic storage device and, if needed, a certified copy of 
same may be obtained from the Office of the Town Clerk.

MOVER: Robert Kern, Councilman

AYES: Hubbard, Rothwell, Kern, Merrifield, Waski

NOTICE OF ADOPTION  
PLEASE TAKE NOTICE, that the Town Board of the Town of Riverhead adopted 
a local law to amend Chapter 231 of the Riverhead Town Code titled “Fire Prevention”, 
Section 7 thereof, “Definitions” at its regular meeting held on May 21, 2025. 
The intent of the proposed amendment is to provide definitions for certain terms added to 
this Chapter of the Town Code 
 A copy of the entire text of the adopted local law may be reviewed at the Office of 
the Town Clerk, 4 West Second Street, Riverhead, New York 11901, between the hours 
of 8:30 a.m. and 4:30 p.m., Monday through Friday and can be accessed on the Town 
of Riverhead website at: www.townofriverheadny.gov under the Agenda and Minutes for 
the May 21, 2025 Town Board Meeting.  
 
Dated:  Riverhead, New York 
         May 21, 2025  
 
   BY ORDER OF THE TOWN BOARD 
                                                      OF THE TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
                                                  JAMES M. WOOTEN, Town Clerk 
 
10.31.a
Packet Pg. 120
Attachment: NOTICE OF ADOPTION CHAPTER 231.7  Fire Prevention (Definitions)  (2025-451 : Adopts a Local Law to Amend Chapter 231.7 Fire
 
 
Chapter 231. Fire Prevention 
Article II. Terminology 
 
§ 231-7. Definitions. 
Unless otherwise expressly stated, the following terms shall, for the purpose of this chapter, have 
the meanings indicated in this section: 
 
Bonfire/Recreational Fire - An outdoor fire burning wood materials where the fuel being burned 
is not contained in an outdoor fireplace or barbecue grill and has a total fuel area of 30 inches or 
less in diameter and 24 inches or less in height from natural grade for pleasure, rel igious, 
ceremonial, cooking, warmth or similar purposes. 
 
Burn Permit – A permit obtained from the Town of Riverhead Fire Marshal’s Office for opening 
burning of agricultural materials associated with a commercial operation. 
 
Bonfire Permit – A permit obtained from the Town of Riverhead Fire Marshal’s Office for use of 
a firepit on Town Property or Commercial Property. 
 
Fire Extinguishing Source – A method of extinguishing an outdoor fire to include a fire 
extinguisher, water can, water bucket or garden hose. 
 
Unapproved Combustible Fuels – Combustible fuels that are not permitted to be burned in outdoor 
fires to include: trash or garbage; plastic, glass or metal items (tin and aluminum cans); pressure -
treated lumber or plywood; painted or stained wood products; construction debris.  
 
Hazardous Materials (HAZMAT) - Substances that can be a threat to the environment or human 
health. These substances can be solids, liquids, or gases, and include but not limited to:  explosives, 
thermal decomposition of batteries ie. thermal runaway, flammable liquids and solids, combustible 
liquids, various types of gas, heavy metals, such as lead, mercury, cadmium, arsenic, and chromium,  
volatile organic compounds (VOCs), such as benzene, toluene, and ethylbenzene, semi volatile 
organic compounds (SVOCs), such as phenols and other components of creosote and coal and 
radioactive materials.  
 
Underline represents addition(s) 
Strikethrough represents deletion(s)

Attachment: NOTICE OF ADOPTION CHAPTER 231.24  Fire Prevention (Reset Alarm Sign)  (2025-452 : Adopts a Local Law to Amend Chapter
Chapter 231. Fire Prevention 
Article VII. Fire Department Access and Operations 
 
§ 231-24 Interference with Fire Department, Fire Marshal or CEO. 
C.  No person shall reset a fire alarm in a commercial or multifamily building without approval from the Fire 
Chief, Fire Marshal, Fire Department Officer in Charge, or Code Enforcement Official. 
(1)  A sign, approved by the Riverhead Fire Marshal, shall be posted by the fire alarm panel stating that 
the fire alarm shall not be reset without the approval of the Fire Chief as set forth in § 231-24 (C) above. 
(2)  This provision, § 231-24 (C), shall exclude single-and two-family dwellings.

a local law to amend Chapter 231 of the Riverhead Town Code titled “Fire Prevention”, 
Section 14 thereof titled, “Assistance to Authorized Agencies; reimbursement of

10.33.a
Packet Pg. 128
Attachment: NOTICE OF ADOPTION CHAPTER 231.14  Fire Prevention (Battery Storage Spills)  (2025-453 : Adopts a Local Law to Amend
Chapter 231. Fire Prevention 
Article IV. Mitigation of Hazardous Condition or 
Occurrence 
 
§ 231-14 Assistance to authorized agencies; reimbursement of expenses 
 
C. The person or entity responsible for the spill, discharge or other release of any hazardous 
material that creates any hazardous condition or occurrence as described in § 231-14 above 
shall be responsible to reimburse the Town for all expenses incurred by the Town for the 
mitigation and investigation of the hazardous condition or occurrence. This section shall 
not apply to accidental spills or releases of home heating oil, residential swimming pool 
treatments or similar materials within or on the premises of owner-occupied single-family 
dwellings, unless such spill or release was due to a negligent or intentional act. This section 
shall apply to the use or storage of lithium-ion batteries and battery installations that 
contain flammable electrolytes and hazardous devices i.e. fireproof and heat resistant fire 
extinguisher blanket. 
 
 
Underline represents addition(s) 
Strikethrough represents deletion(s)

Attachment: NOTICE OF ADOPTION CHAPTER 231.38  Fire Prevention (Flammable Liquids Gas Pumps)  (2025-454 : Adopts a Local Law to
Chapter 231. Fire Prevention 
Article XIV. Flammable and Combustible Liquids 
§ 231-38. Applicability. 
A. This article shall apply to the storage, handling and use of flammable liquids as defined in 
Article II, except that it shall not apply to the transportation of flammable liquids when in 
conformity with regulations of the Federal and State Departments of Transportation or 
regulations lawfully on file with and approved by the Federal and State Departments of 
Transportation. 
 
B. New and existing installations of flammable motor fuel dispensing systems shall have and 
maintain an automatic fire-extinguishing system using an extinguishing agent suitable for 
petroleum fires and installed in accordance with NFPA 17 and their listings, and UL 1254 
Standard for Pre -Engineered Dry Chemical Extinguishing systems. The fire protection 
system shall be connected to the fire alarm system, if provided, in accordance with the 
requirements of NFPA 72. 
 
C. The proposed Article XIV §231-38(B) is enacted pursuant to Municipal Home Rule Law 
§ 10(1)(ii)(a)(11), (12) and (14);

10.35.a
Packet Pg. 136
Attachment: NOTICE OF ADOPTION CHAPTER 231.25  Fire Prevention (Outdoor Fires)  (2025-455 : Adopts a Local Law to Amend Chapter
 
 
Chapter 231. Fire Prevention 
Article VIII. Precautions Against Fire 
 
§ 231-25. Outdoor fires. 
A. Permit required. 
(1) No person shall ignite or maintain any outdoor fire, except a fire used exclusively to 
cook food for human consumption, without first having obtained a burn permit from the 
Town Fire Marshal and any other required agency. 
(2) No person shall kindle or maintain an outdoor fire to be unsafe or hazard -producing as 
determined by the Fire Chief, Fire Marshal, State Forest Ranger or state, county or Town 
police officer, who may immediately suspend or revoke any burn permit previously  
issued. 
B. Who may prohibit. The Chief of the Fire Department or the Fire Marshal may prohibit any or 
all bonfires and outdoor rubbish fires when atmospheric conditions, drought or unfavorable 
weather conditions or local circumstances make such fires hazardous. 
 
A.    No person shall kindle, maintain, authorize or permit any bonfires, recreational fires or open 
burning on or in any street, alley, road, land or public grounds or upon any private lot, unless 
conducted in accordance with this section and with the Building and Fire Code of New York 
State and New York Code Rules and Regulations Title 6 New York State Department of 
Environmental Conservation. Chapter III Part 215.  
Fires that are used to dispose of  flags or religious items that are used in connection with a 
religious ceremony as defined in the Fire Code of New York State shall be considered exempt 
from this subsection upon satisfactory proof and/or testimony.  
(1) Residential Property 
a. No Permit required. 
i. Notwithstanding A (1)(a) above, n o person shall kindle or maintain any 
bonfire on any privately owned property without adhering to the following 
provisions: 
1. No fire shall be kindled or maintained unless it is a minimum of 25 
feet from any building or structure;  
2. No fire shall be left unattended 
3. No fire be kindled or maintained if the prevailing wind exceeds a 
velocity of 15 miles per hour 
4. No fire shall be kindled or maintained as to create or cause to be 
created any noxious or offensive odor or smoke as to be hazard -
producing 
10.35.b
Packet Pg. 137
Attachment: 231.25 Outdoor Fires  (2025-455 : Adopts a Local Law to Amend Chapter 231.25 Fire Prevention (Outdoor Fires))
 
 
5. No fire shall be kindled or maintained unless adequate provisions 
are made to prevent the spread of fire 
6. No fire shall be kindled or maintained without an appropriate fire 
extinguishing source   
7. No fire shall be kindled or maintained unless in an approved above-
ground fire pit or a permanent in-ground fire pit 
8. No fire shall be kindled or maintained with any combustible fuels 
other than dry, plain, untreated wood. All other fuels are considered 
unapproved combustibles fuels. 
 
This shall in no way be construed as applicable to barbeque grills, outdoor 
fireplaces or gas-fueled fire pits 
(2) Commercial Property 
a. Permit required 
i. No person shall kindle or maintain any bonfire fire without first having 
obtained a burn permit from the Town of Riverhead Fire Marshal’s Office. 
(3) Town of Riverhead Property 
a. Permit Required  
i. No person shall kindle of maintain any bonfire on Town of Riverhead 
property without first having obtained a bonfire permit from the Town of 
Riverhead Fire Marshal’s Office. 
 
B.   No person shall kindle or maintain any outdoor fire determined to be unsafe or hazard-producing 
as set forth in § 231-25 and as determined by the Fire Chief, Fire Marshal, Code Enforcement 
Officer and/or State Forest Ranger or state, county or town police officer and such official may 
immediately suspend or revoke any permit previously issued. 
 
C.   Who may prohibit. The Fire Chief or Fire Marshal, may prohibit any or all bonfires and outdoor 
fires or open burning when atmospheric conditions, drought or  other unfavorable weather 
conditions or local circumstances make such fires hazardous.

Packet Pg. 141
Attachment: NOTICE OF ADOPTION CHAPTER 231.66 Fire Prevention (Penalties)  (2025-456 : Adopts a Local Law to Amend Chapter 231.66 Fire
Chapter 231. Fire Prevention 
Article XXIV. Penalties for Offenses 
§ 231-66 Penalties for offenses; notice of violation. 
A. Any person who shall violate any of the provisions of this chapter or fail to comply with the 
provisions thereof, or who shall violate or fail to comply with any order made thereunder, except 
for § 231-55 shall be guilty of a misdemeanor, punishable by a fine of not less than $250 nor 
more than $2,500 or by imprisonment for not more than 15 days, or by both such fine and 
imprisonment. 
B. The imposition of a penalty for any violation shall not excuse the violation or allow it to 
continue, and all such persons shall be required to correct or remedy such violations or defects 
within a reasonable time, and when not otherwise specified, a separate offense shall be deemed 
committed for each day that the prohibited conditions are maintained following receipt of a 
notice from the Fire Marshal or CEO identifying the violation and requiring its correction. Said 
notice shall be mailed to the owner, at his or her mailing address as listed on the Town's most 
recent tax roll, by certified mail, return-receipt requested. 
C. A civil penalty in the amount of $500 shall be imposed for each violation of Article V of this 
chapter. 
D. Any person who shall violate § 231-55 of this chapter shall be guilty of a violation level 
offense, punishable by a fine of not less than $250 nor more than $2,500 or by imprisonment for 
not more than 15 days, or by both such fine and imprisonment. 
 
Underline represents addition(s) 
Strikethrough represents deletion(s)

ASSESSES COST OF LABOR & MATERIAL FOR PREVIOUSLY AUTHORIZED

Councilman Rothwell offered the following resolution,

WHEREAS, pursuant to Resolution #2024-864 adopted by the Riverhead Town

removal of yard waste, rubbish, litter, garbage/refuse and all weeds, noxious plants, 
grass and/or rank vegetation in excess of ten (10) inches in height at the premises 
located at 12 Longview Drive, Riverhead, New York, known and designated as Suffolk 
County Tax Map as 0600-014.00-02.00-012.000; and 
 
WHEREAS, the Town of Riverhead Engineering Department did seek estimates 
for this property clean-up from four (4) potential vendors and upon receipt of two (2) 
response, determined that Correct Construction, Inc. was the lowest responsible 
estimate; and 
 
WHEREAS, on March 28, 2025, Correct Construction, Inc. under the oversight of 
the Riverhead Town Engineering Department appeared at the real property at 12 
Longview Drive, Riverhead, New York, known and designated as Suffolk County Tax 
Map as 0600-014.00-02.00-012.000 and conducted and completed work required to 
facilitate the removal yard waste, rubbish, litter, garbage/refuse and all weeds, noxious 
plants, grass and/or rank vegetation in excess of ten (10) inches in height; and 
 
  WHEREAS, by Resolution #2024-864 adopted on October 16, 2024 and 
pursuant to Chapter 251.25 of the Riverhead Town Code, the Riverhead Town Board 
directed that all costs and expenses incurred by the Town in furtherance of removing all 
yard waste, rubbish, litter, garbage/refuse and all weeds, noxious plants, grass and/or 
rank vegetation in excess of ten (10) inches in height be reported and shall constitute a 
lien against the premises and assessed against the owner of the property; and 
 
WHEREAS, the costs and expenses incurred by the Town of Riverhead in 
furtherance of removing all yard waste, rubbish, litter, garbage/refuse and all weeds, 
noxious plants, grass and/or rank vegetation in excess of ten (10) inches in height at the 
premises at 12 Longview Drive, Riverhead, New York, known and designated as Suffolk 
County Tax Map as 0600-014.00-02.00-012.000 is $8,580.50 and documentation 
supporting such sum is attached herewith. 
 
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that based upon the foregoing, the 
Town Board of the Town of Riverhead hereby directs that the sum of $8,580.50 shall be 
charged against and assessed to the real property at 12 Longview Drive, Riverhead,

TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
 
TB Resolution 2025-458 
 
RIVERHEAD TOWN BOARD SUPPORTS THE DEVELOPMENT OF A YMCA 
RECREATION FACILITY AT THE FORMER NEW YORK STATE ARMORY AND 
AUTHORIZES THE OFFICE OF THE TOWN ATTORNEY TO SEEK AMENDMENT OF 
ORIGINAL BILL S04404/A06825, INCLUDING HOME RULE REQUEST, TO 
AUTHORIZE LEASE OR SALE TO THE YMCA OF LONG ISLAND 
 
Councilman Kern offered the following resolution, 
which was seconded by Councilwoman Merrifield 
 
WHEREAS, the New York State, by S04404/A06825 “Relates to the conveyance 
of land formerly used as an armory to the town of Riverhead in the county of Suffolk” 
and signed into law by the Governor on August 31, 2022 (Laws of the State of New 
York 2011, Chapter 495) transferred the 5.72 -acre former  New York State Armory 
facility, including a structure of approximately 32,101 square feet to the Town of  
Riverhead in 2011; and  
   
WHEREAS, the Assembly and Senate Bills referenced above and, significantly, 
the Laws of the State of New York, Chapter 495  provided the “[a]ny lands transferred 
pursuant to this act shall be used for  the purposes  of  the  Town of Riverhead to utilize 
the subject property and improve the structures for use by the police department, justice  
court,  public  safety  and  recreational programs developed and operated by the Town 
of Riverhead police department and upon  termination  of  such  use, title to the lands so 
transferred shall revert to the state of New York”; and 
 
WHEREAS, despite various attempts, the Town of Riverhead has been unable to 
repurpose the former Armory for improvement and use by the police department, justice 
court, public safety and/or recreational programs developed and operated by the 
Riverhead Police Department as set forth in the enabling state legislation; and 
 
WHEREAS, the Town did acquire a new Town Hall at 4 West Second Street, 
Riverhead, NY, the Town determined that it is most cost effective and has committed to 
renovate the building previously used as the Town Hall at 200 Howell Avenue, 
Riverhead, NY into a new Justice Court thereby permitting the Police Department at 210 
Howell Avenue to recapture the space currently occupied by the Justice Court facility, 
and as a result thereof, the former New York State Armory facility, is no longer needed 
for those uses as set forth in the Laws of 2011, c. 495, with the exception of the ongoing 
need for space dedicated recreation and community programs; and  
   
WHEREAS, while there continues to be a tremendous need for recreation and 
community services for young and old alike in the Town and the proximity of the Armory 
to Stotkzy Park are ideally suited and will compliment recreation and programs offered 
at Stotkzy Park, the Town does not have the funding to undertake the necessary 
renovations of the former New York State Armory facility, now in a state of blight,  nor 
10.38
Packet Pg. 154
funds to operate, manage or maintain such an expansion of its recreational programs; 
and 
 
WHEREAS, YMCA of Long Island  leaders have toured the Armory site with 
Town of Riverhead staff and expressed interest in leasing or purchasing the Armory site 
from the Town for a variety of uses all centered and focused on well-being, including but 
not limited to, fitness and health, education, designed for and spanning ages from pre -
school/early childhood, children, pre-teen and teen programs, adults and older adults for 
local and county residents; and 
 
WHEREAS, the proposed Lessor or Purchaser, YMCA of Long Island, is an 
organization with a mission to build and develop principles of respect, responsibility, and 
caring with programs to build healthy spirits, mind and body in all members throughout 
the numerous communities served by the YMCA; and 
 
WHEREAS, YMCA of Long Island has and continues to successfully serve 
communities on Long Island, including but not limited to Huntington, Glen Cove, 
Patchogue, and other communities and has become an integral resource for such 
communities; and 
 
WHEREAS, the YMCA’s primary use and improvements for the former Amory 
include, but are not limited to, a children’s room, multi -purpose rooms, community 
kitchen, co -working space, STEM lab, teen room, gymnasium, indoor track, sports 
courts, multi -purpose exercise studios, fitness area, adult locker rooms, youth locker 
rooms, aquatics, administration offices, and multi-purpose classroom space; and  
 
   
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Riverhead Town Board hereby 
enthusiastically supports the development of a YMCA recreation facility at the former 
New York State Armory and approves the Office of the Town Attorney to advocate for 
and work with local State officials to make an amendment to the 2011 Laws of the New 
York State to authorize the lease or sale to the YMCA for uses described as  recreation 
and community services for young and old alike in the Town, subject to a reverter 
clause, with the purpose and intent to service the residents of Riverhead and any further 
agreement shall be drafted by the office of the Town Attorney for approval by the Town 
Board; and  
 
BE IT FURTHER, RESOLVED,  at such time as appropriate, the Office of the 
Town Attorney shall prepare a Municipal Home Rule Request and after preparation, the 
Supervisor and/or Town Clerk, as the case may be, shall be authorized to execute 
same; and 
 
BE IT FURTHER, RESOLVED, that the Town Clerk be and is hereby authorized 
to forward a copy of this resolution to the Office of the Town Attorney, and State 
Assemblywoman Jodi Giglio  giglioj2@nyassembly.gov and State Senator Anthony 
Palumbo palumbo@nysenate.gov; and 
   
BE IT FURTHER, RESOLVED, that all Town Hall Departments may review and 
obtain a copy of this resolution from the electronic storage device, and, if needed, a 
certified copy of same can be obtained from the office of the Town Clerk.

ISSUES RESPONSES TO COMMENTS ON CONDITIONAL NEGATIVE

Councilwoman Merrifield offered the following resolution,

WHEREAS, the Riverhead Town Board is in receipt of a site plan application 
seeking to amend the previously approved site plan of Island Water Park (d/b/a Scott’s 
Pointe); and  
 
WHEREAS, proposed amendments include legalization of a go -kart track, 
pickleball courts, and conversion of an existing interior storage space for use as a 
catering/event space; and  
 
WHEREAS, by Resolution No. 2024-996, adopted December 17, 2024, the Town 
Board classified the action as an Unlisted action pursuant to SEQRA, and commenced 
coordinated review among involved agencies; and  
 
 WHEREAS¸ by Resolution No. 2025 -234, dated March 4, 2025, the Town Board 
issued a Conditional Negative Declaration (CND) pursuant to SEQRA, finding that the 
proposed action is not anticipated to result in any significant negative environmental 
impacts, with the imposition of the following conditions: 
 
1. The applicant shall submit an as -built, topographic survey of the pickleball 
courts and go-kart track, and shall submit an amended grading and drainage 
plan demonstrating retention and capture of all stormwater, with same being 
prevented from entering the pond. 
 
2. The use of the track shall be limited to go -karts, as stated by the applicant in 
their submittals, and that the use of the track for any other type of vehicle 
shall be prohibited.  This restriction shall be recorded as a covenant against 
the subject property by the applicant. 
 
3. The applicant shall amend the site plan to identify fuel storage area, shall 
implement spill protection measures, shall maintain on -site a spill response 
kit, and shall proposed a spill response plan in order to capture and contain 
spills of any materials that may occur on site.  
 
4. Groundwater monitoring, as agreed to by the applicant, and as recorded with 
the Suffolk County Clerk on October 31, 2024 under Liber D00013270, Page 
495, shall continue on the property for the duration of the agreement period.

Determination and shall submit the results of the NYSDEC Jurisdictional

 WHEREAS, the notice of the CND was published in the New York State

Board’s formal response to comments on the CND; and be it further,

STAFF REPORT 
 
To:  Tim Hubbard, Town Supervisor 
Town Board Members 
From: Greg Bergman, Senior Planner 
Re: Island Water Park (D/B/A Scott’s Pointe) –  Conditioned Negative Declaration 
Comments and Responses  
 5835 Middle Country Road, Calverton, NY 
SCTM No. 600-135-1-7.34 
Date: May 5, 2025 ______________________________________________________________________________                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  
 
SEQRA History 
 
By Resolution No. 2025-234, dated March 4, 2025, the Town Board issued a Conditional Negative 
Declaration (CND) for the site plan application of Island Water Park, which sought to legalize 
improvements made to an existing commercial site, including constru ction of a go- kart track, 
pickleball courts, and conversion of use of existing interior space for use as catering/event space.   
 
The Notice of CND was posted in the New York State Department of Environmental 
Conservation’s Environmental (NYSDEC) News Bulletin on March 19, 2025.  Pursuant to 6 
NYCRR Part 617.7(d)(1)(iv), a 30 -day public comment period commenced from the date of 
publication of the CND in the ENB.  
 
Comments Received 
 
Three letters (attached) were sent to the Town Clerk in response to the CND, within the 
allowable time-frame, as follows: 
 
1. Letter from Barbara Blass, dated March 31, 2025. 
2. Letter from Jenn Hartnagel, on behalf of Group for the East End, dated March 17, 2025. 
3. Letter from Barbara Blass, dated April 11, 2025.  
 
Dawn C. Thomas, Esq. Greg Bergman Matt Charters Heather Trojanowski             vacant 
Economic Development, 
Planning and Building 
Administrator 
Ext. 287 
Senior Planner 
Ext. 264 
Senior Planner 
Ext. 207 
             Planner 
             Ext. 283 
Principal Office Assistant 
Ext. 240 
 
10.39.a
Packet Pg. 162
Attachment: Island Water Park - CND Response Report 5.5.25  (2025-459 : Island Water Park CND Response)
Island Water Park (D/B/A Scott’s Pointe) – CND Comments and Responses 
2 
 
Pursuant to SEQRA, the Lead Agency is required to review all comments received during the 
public comment period to determine if they raise substantive issues and are relevant to the 
adequacy of the CND (SEQR Handbook, Page 91). 
 
Substantive Comments 
 
Staff review of the above referenced letters identifies the following substantive comments: 
 
Comment 1:  Barbara Blass, April 11, 2025:  “Did the environmental review adequately identify 
and evaluate noise from the go karts as a potential negative impact on birds and 
other species in the grasslands and woodlands proximate to the track?  The 
NYSDEC has identified April 23 through August 15 as a bird breeding and nesting 
period during which certain activities are restricted.  Should the CND conditions 
be modified to restrict the operation of gas powered go-karts during this period?  
Should the CND be modified to include a noise barrier or require electric go-karts 
in the alternative?  
 
Response 1: NYSDEC guidance, as provided for in the NYSDEC Strategy for Grassland Bird 
Habitat Management and Conservation 2022 -2027 Manual 
(https://dec.ny.gov/sites/default/files/2024-04/grasslandbirdsstrategyfinal.pdf) 
do not identify any targeted Grassland Bird Con servation Centers in the vicinity 
of the project site. It is acknowledged, however, that there is grassland habitat 
identified in the June 3, 2014 Habitat Protection Plan for Enterprise Park at 
Calverton, prepared by VHB Engineering, Surveying & Landscape Architecture.  
The proximity from the go-kart track to nearest portion of the identified grassland 
habitats along the western runway at EPCAL is approximately 1,150 feet .  Given 
the separation distance, and the presence of significant existing wooded buffers 
between the grassland habitats and the go-kart track, sound levels from the track 
are not expected to result in significant impacts to these areas.  Furthermore, 
NYSDEC did not raise this as an issue in their SEQR coordination response letter, 
dated January 29, 2025, which was received during the SEQR coordination period.   
 
Comment 2: Jenn Hartnagel, Group for the East End, March 17, 2025:  “Condition 6 in the 
CND states, “The applicant must receive approval from the Suffolk County 
Department of Health Services (SCDOH) Office of Wastewater Management…”  
According to the SEQRA Handbook (Edition 4), a lead agency cannot require, as a 
condition, approval from another agency because it is not a mitigative measure.  
The Handbook states, “Furthermore, a CND cannot be used to create an approval 
authority for an agency that has no esta blished jurisdiction over the proposed 
action” (p.96)”  
 
Response 2: Comment acknowledged.  Pursuant to the SEQR handbook, the Town Board, as 
Lead Agency, cannot rely on a CND to attach conditions that are explicitly 
articulated standards (either numerical or narrative) within that lead agency's 
underlying jurisdiction, or conditions that an applicant is otherwise legally 
obligated to meet in order to obtain a permit or approval, such as meeting emission 
or discharge standards, as required by law (SEQR Handbook, Page 92)  
10.39.a
Packet Pg. 163
Attachment: Island Water Park - CND Response Report 5.5.25  (2025-459 : Island Water Park CND Response)
Island Water Park (D/B/A Scott’s Pointe) – CND Comments and Responses 
3 
 
 
Thus, the CND shall be modified to remove the requirements of receiving Suffolk 
County Department of Health Services approval, as well as the need for the 
Freshwater Wetland Parcel Jurisdictional Determination (JD) by the NYSDEC, as 
these are conditions that the applicant is otherwise legally obligated to meet in 
order to obtain a permit or approval.  
 
Comment 3: Barbara Blass, March 31, 2025: “SEQRA guidance document indicates a CND 
should never rely on a future investigation to develop conditions of mitigation.  The 
mitigating conditions must be explicitly defined when the CND is issued.  This 
CND relies on future investigation by an Involved Agency, the DEC.”  
 
Response 3: Comment acknowledged.  Pursuant to the SEQR handbook, the Town Board, as 
Lead Agency, cannot rely on a CND to attach conditions that are explicitly 
articulated standards (either numerical or narrative) within that lead agency's 
underlying jurisdiction, or conditions that an applicant is otherwise legally 
obligated to meet in order to obtain a permit or approval, such as meeting emission 
or discharge standards, as required by law (SEQR Handbook, Page 92)  
 
Thus, the CND shall be modified to remove the requirements of receiving Suffolk 
County Department of Health Services approval, as well as the need for the 
Freshwater Wetland Parcel Jurisdictional Determination (JD) by the NYSDEC, as 
these are conditions th at the applicant is otherwise legally obligated to meet in 
order to obtain a permit or approval.  
 
Other Comments and Responses  
 
Both Jenn Har tnagel’s letter, dated March 17, 2025, and Barbara Blass’s letter, dated March 31, 
2025, make reference to general SEQR process, specifically the Unlisted classification of the 
proposed action, with both letters citing Riverhead Town Code §225-11B(5) as a compelling factor 
that requires the action to be classified as a Type I action pursuant to SEQR. 
 
Town Code §225 -11B(5) states that “parking facilities or other facilities with an associated 
parking area where the total number of parking spaces if 50 spaces or greater,” are considered a 
Type I action pursuant to SEQR.  This section of code was not drafted to capture any action on a 
site containing 50 or more parking stalls, but rather, was intended to classify the construction of 
new parking facilities with 50 or more parking stalls.  A s trict interpretation of this section to 
mean any action on a site containing 50 or more parking stalls would mean that  minor actions 
such as façade renovations or changes from one permitted use to another permitted use within a 
specific zoning district would be considered Type I actions, when they are in fact Type II actions 
(6a7.5(c)(2) and 617.5(c)(18), respectively). 
 
The Town Board’s classification of the Island Water Park site plan amendments is accurate  and 
need not be amended.   
 
 
 
10.39.a
Packet Pg. 164
Attachment: Island Water Park - CND Response Report 5.5.25  (2025-459 : Island Water Park CND Response)
Island Water Park (D/B/A Scott’s Pointe) – CND Comments and Responses 
4 
 
Next Steps 
 
Per the SEQR handbook , if comments are received that suggest improvements to an already 
adequate mitigation measure or a better way to mitigate the impact, the lead agency has the 
discretion to make a minor adjustment to the CND.  This type of minor revision to address 
comments that will strengthen an already adequate mitigation measure would not require that 
the lead agency go through the CND process again or require the preparation of a draft EIS.  The 
lead agency may, as indicated in the first option above, choose to respond  to the comment by 
stating the revision that was made to the CND (SEQR Handbook, Page 91).  
 
Staff recommends the Town Board adopt a resolution accepting this staff report and the 
comments contained herein as constituting the Board’s responses to comments submitted on the 
CND, and make clarification in the resolution that conditions regarding the removal of the 
SCDOH and NYSDEC requirements as conditions of the CND.  Although these items are not 
specific to a mitigation, and do not necessarily strengthen a specific mitigation measure, they 
should be removed as the applicant is already legally obligated to meet the requirements in order 
to obtain a permit or approval.

 WHEREAS, in a letter dated January 31, 2025, the Suffolk County Planning

1. Pursuant to NYS General Municipal Law §239 and Suffolk County 
Administrative Code §A14-14, actions subject to referral include the adoption 
or amendment of a comprehensive plan, zoning ordinance or local law, the 
issuance of a special use permit, approval of a site plan, the granting of area 
or use variances or other authorizations prior to making a final determination.  
Site plan such as the ones dated 11/18/21 should have been referred to the 
Suffolk County Planning Commission before being approved by the Town. 
 
2. Though the outdoor go -kart track and pickleball courts appear to have been 
constructed between March and June of 2024 , the applicant should be 
encouraged to incorporate green methodologies such as rain gardens, 
bioswales, etc. as described in the Suffolk County Planning Commission

3. Whenever possible commercial buildings should incorporate the use of

4. Information pertaining to a proposed lighting plan for the go -cart track and

10.40
Packet Pg. 167
Be advised, this agency does not accept or process applications for existing 
structures and we do not issue after -the-fact permits for existing structures located 
within regulated areas.  Structures built within a regulated area without benefit of a 
DEC permit is either a violation of the Environmental Conservation Law (ECL) or it 
did not require a permit.  Permits must be obtained prior to any work activities taking 
place. 
 
On April 11, 2023, DEC received a Mining Permit Application requesting renewal of 
an Article 23 permit as the property owner required additional time for reclamation 
efforts.  DEC may have additional comments at a later date as this application is 
currently undergoing technical review. 
 
DEC has the following comments: 
 
1. If this event space is new or otherwise not included on the SPDES application 
being reviewed by Suffolk County Department of Health Services, the permit 
would need modification before Island Water Park is authorized to discharge 
wastewater from this portion of the project. 
 
2. Portion of New York State regulated freshwater wetlands and their adjacent 
areas may be located in the project area.  Although some limited activities are 
exempt from permitting, most activities that involve disturbance within a 
wetland or its 100 -foot adjacent area require an Environmental Conservation 
Law (ECL) Article 24, Freshwater Wetlands permit from the DEC.  Information 
on regulated activities within freshwater wetlands and adjacent areas is 
available on DEC’s website (see Regulated Activities), which contains 
examples of regulated activities and those exempt from wetland permits.  
 
DEC’s amended Article 24, Freshwater Wetlands Jurisdiction and Classification 
regulations (6 NYCRR Part 664) went into effect on January 1, 2025.  To 
determine whether the property contains regulated freshwater wetlands, the 
project sponsor must submit a request for a Parcel Jurisdictional Determination 
(Parcel JD).  A Parcel JD is a determination made by DEC whether a property 
contains regulated freshwater wetlands or adjacent areas within the parcel 
boundary.  Please use the attached link to request a Parcel JD for the project 
site: https://dec.ny.gov/nature/waterbodies/wetlands/freshwater-wetlands-
program/freshwater-wetland-jurisdictional-determination.  If you have any 
problems submitting the Parcel JD request, please email: 
fwwjurisdiction@dec.ny.gov. 
 
If the property contains regulated freshwater wetlands or adjacent areas, further 
delineation of the wetland boundaries and a Project Jurisdictional Determination 
(Project JD) may be required.  A Project JD is a determination made by DEC 
whether a proposed activity within a parcel containing regulated freshwater 
wetlands or adjacent areas requires an Article 24 Freshwater Wetlands permit.  If 
necessary, a Project JD may also be requested using the link provided above.  If 
regulated freshwater wetlands or ad jacent areas are present, all efforts must be 
made to first avoid disturbing the wetland and adjacent area.  If disturbance to 
the wetland and/or adjacent area cannot be avoided, the project sponsor must 
submit a Freshwater Wetland permit application, and obtain a permit to conduct a 
regulated activity.  In accordance with DEC’s Freshwater Wetlands Permit 
Requirements Regulations (6 NYCRR Part 663), the applicant would need to 
10.40
Packet Pg. 168
justify the disturbance, discuss alternatives and minimize impacts as part of the 
Freshwater Wetlands permit application.  More information on application 
procedures and permit issuance standards is available on ’EC's website at: 
https://dec.ny.gov/regulatory/permits-licenses/waterways-coastlines-
wetlands/freshwater-wetlands#Determnine. 
 
3. DEC has concerns regarding the possibility of spillage from the track to enter 
surface waters.  Since this would be an unintended and intermittent 
discharge, it is not something that DEC would regulate under a SPDES 
Permit.  Instead, this would likely be handled on a case -by-case basis with 
possible violations if/when these discharges were to occur.  To avoid potential 
violations, DEC suggests the applicant implement Best Management 
Practices around the track/edge of water to further reduce the risk for 
anything running off of the track an into the water; and  
 
WHEREAS, in a letter dated January 3, 2025, the Suffolk County Department of 
Health Services had the following comments: 
 
1. Sanitary Code: 
 
A: Article VI Application Status : The Department has not received a commercial 
wastewater application for the above referenced project, as required by Article VI 
of the Suffolk County Sanitary Code.  The project sponsor should submit an 
application to our agency’s Office of Wastewater Management at the earliest 
possible date so that a complete technical assessment of this proposal can be 
undertaken. 
 
B.  SCDHS Jurisdiction :  The SCDHS maintains jurisdiction over the final use 
and size of the property.  The applicant, therefore, should not undertake the 
subdivision without Health Department approval.  Density and complete site plan 
details are essential to the review of this project.  These considerations are 
reviewed completely at the time of SCDHS application; and  
 
 WHEREAS, in a letter dated February 25, 2025, the Chief Fire Marshal had the 
following comments: 
 
1. Emergency Responder radio coverage system must be completed in existing 
building. 
 
2. An additional fire hydrant will be required if there is an exterior storage for 
flammable gas further than 400 feet from existing hydrant. 507.1 Required 
Water Supply – An approved water supply capable of supplying the required 
fire flow for fire protection shall be provided to premises on which facilities, 
building or portions of buildings are hereafter constructed or moved into or 
within the jurisdiction.  FACILITY. A building or use in a fixed location 
including exterior storage areas for flammable and combustible substances 
and hazardous materials, piers, wharves, tank farms and similar uses.  This 
term includes recreational vehicles, mobile home and manufactured housing 
parks, sales and storage lots.  
 
3. Proprietor must comply with NFPA610 standard for emergency and safety 
operations at motorsports venues; and 
10.40
Packet Pg. 169
 
WHEREAS¸ in an email dated January 24, 2025, D&B Engineers indicated that 
the proposed improvements, including go -kart track and pickleball courts are still 
covered under the existing Stormwater Pollution Prevention Plan Waiver; and  
 
WHEREAS, in a memo dated May 14, 2025, the Town Engineer had the 
following comments: 
 
1. Please provide a barrier around the outside of the track where the track is 
adjacent to the lake. This measure shall be designed to prevent any 
discharges from the track or surrounding earthen area to the lake. Discharges 
to a surface water body of the state which cause deterioration of the water 
body are a violation of NYS Environmental Conservation Law; and  
 
WHEREAS¸ the applicant has submitted a Spill Prevention and Response Plan, 
prepared by JRH Consulting Engineers, DPC, dated April 2025, as required by the 
CND; and  
 
 WHEREAS, the Town Board has considered the site plan application, the SEQR 
record, comments received at the public hearing, and all other relevant planning, 
zoning, and environmental factors.   
 
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED,  that the Town Board hereby grants 
preliminary site plan approval for the site plan application of Island Water Park (d/b/a 
Scott’s Pointe), including a site plan, prepared and stamped by James R. Holzmacher, 
PE, last dated April 10, 2025, with sheets labeled C-1: Existing Site Plan, C-2: Proposed 
Site Plan, C-3: Parking Layout Plan and Calcs, C -4: Grading and Drainage Plan, C -4.1: 
Existing Pickleball and Go -Kart Topo Plan, C -5: Lighting & Landscape Plan; and be it 
further, 
 
 RESOLVED, that as the applicant has already received the requisite approvals 
from the Suffolk County Department of Health Services Office of Wastewater 
Management, Building Permits and Fire Marshal permits  for the interior catering/event 
space can issue; and be it further, 
 
 RESOLVED¸ that no Certificates of Occupancy for the interior catering/event 
space shall issue until successful completion of all necessary Building and Fire Marshal 
permits relative to the interior catering/event space , and payment of necessary Key 
Money to the Riverhead Water District, as detailed in their November 25, 2024 letter; 
and be it further, 
 
RESOLVED, that prior to final site plan approval, the following conditions shall be 
satisfied: 
 
2. The applicant must obtain a Freshwater Wetlands Jurisdictional 
Determination from the NYSDEC. 
 
3. The applicant must fully reclaim the mine under NYSDEC Permit ID 1-4730-
01022/00002, and provide certification to the Town of Riverhead that the mine 
has been closed out. 
 
4. The applicant shall satisfy the Chief Fire Marshal’s comments from letter 
10.40
Packet Pg. 170
dated February 25, 2025. 
 
5. The site plan shall be amended to include a barrier around the outside of the 
track to control stormwater management and erosion into the lake, as detailed 
in the Town Engineer’s May 14, 2025 memo. 
 
6. The applicant must resolve any outstanding violations with the NYSDEC 
relative to the site improvements which were made without benefit of a permit 
from the NYSDEC.  
 
7. The applicant shall file a covenant on the property, in a form approved by the 
Town Attorney, restricting the use of the track to go -karts, and that use of the 
track for any other type of vehicles shall be prohibited; and be it further, 
 
RESOLVED, that the Town Clerk is hereby authorized to forward a certified copy 
of this resolution to the Ken Myers ( ken@scottspointe.com), the Building Department, 
the Town Attorney’s office; and be it further 
 
 RESOLVED, that all Town Hall Departments may review and obtain a copy of 
this resolution from the electronic storage device and if needed, a certified copy of same 
may be obtained from the Office of the Town Clerk.

ARTICLE XLV - SECTION 108-254 PROCEDURE1.ALL APPLICATIONS FOR SITE PLAN REVIEW, USE PERMITS, PLANNED UNIT DEVELOPMENTS, SUBDIVISION APPROVALS, APPLICABLE SIGN PERMITS,OR BUILDING PERMITS SHALL INCLUDE LIGHTING PLANS SHOWING LOCATION OF EACH EXISTING AND PROPOSED OUTDOOR LIGHT FIXTURE, ANDLUMINAIRE DISTRIBUTION, TYPE, LAMP SOURCE TYPE, WATTAGE, MOUNTING HEIGHT, HOURS OF OPERATION. LUMEN OUTPUT, AND ILLUMINANCELEVELS IN TEN-FOOT GRIDS IN ORDER TO VERIFY THAT LIGHTING CONFORMS TO THE PROVISION OF THIS ARTICLE. THE PLANNING DIRECTORMAY WAIVE THE REQUIREMENTS FOR ILLUMINACE LEVEL INFORMATION ONLY, IF THE TOWN ENGINEER FINDS THAT THE ILLUMINANCE LEVELSCONFORM TO THIS ARTICLE. FOR ALL OTHER EXTERIOR LIGHTS WHICH MUST CONFORM TO THE REQUIREMENTS OF THIS ARTICLE XLV, ANAPPLICATION SHALL BE MADE TO THE PLANNING BOARD SHOWING LOCATION, LUMINAIRE AND BULB TYPE, HEIGHT, HOURS OF OPERATION,LUMEN OUTPUT AND ILLUMINACE LEVELS. APPLICATIONS FOR SUBDIVISION APPROVAL REGARDING LIGHTING PLANS MUST BE SUBMITTED TOBOTH THE PLANNING DEPARTMENT AND ENGINEERING DEPARTMENT.2.THE PLANNING BOARD SHALL REVIEW ANY NEW EXTERIOR LIGHTING OR ANY EXISTING EXTERIOR LIGHTING ON SUBJECT PROPERTY THAT ISPART OF AN  APPLICATION FOR DESIGN REVIEW, CONDITIONAL USE PERMIT, PLANNED UNIT DEVELOPMENT, SUBDIVISION APPROVAL,APPLICABLE SIGN PERMITS OR BUILDING PERMIT, TO DETERMINE WHETHER THE EXTERIOR LIGHTING COMPLIES WITH THE STANDARDS OF THISARTICLE XLV.3.FOR ALL OTHER EXTERIOR LIGHTING WHICH MUST CONFORM TO THE REQUIREMENTS OF ARTICLE XLV, THE PLANNING BOARD SHALL ISSUE ADECISION WHEATHER THE EXTERIOR LIGHTING COMPLIES WITH THE STANDARDS OF THIS ARTICLE XLV. ALL SUCH DECISIONS MAY BE APPEALEDTO THE TOWN OF RIVERHEAD ZONING BOARD OF APPEALS WITHIN 30 DAYS OF THE DECISION.

TB Resolution 2025-462 
 
AUTHORIZES TOWN CLERK TO PUBLISH AND POST NOTICE TO AMEND 
CHAPTER 301 ZONING AND LAND DEVELOPMENT, PART 3 SUPPLEMENTARY 
USE REGULATIONS, ARTICLE LIIC CANNABIS,  § 301-283.20. LOCATION AND 
NUMBER OF PERMITTED RETAIL AND ON-SITE CONSUMPTION 
ESTABLISHMENTS AND § 301-283.25 WHEN EFFECTIVE 
 
Councilman Kern offered the following resolution, 
which was seconded by Councilwoman Merrifield 
 
WHEREAS, by Local Law No . 23-2022 dated November 11, 2022 the Town 
Board of Town of Riverhead added Article LIIC Cannabis to Chapter 301 Zoning and 
Land Development of the Town Code of the Town of Riverhead which was further 
amended by Local Law No. 12-2024 dated March 5, 2024; and  
 
WHEREAS, the Town Board desires to make further amendments as specified 
within the proposed amendments attached hereto; and  
 
WHEREAS, the proposed amendments are a Type I action pursuant to SEQRA 
(NYCRR 617.4 b (2)); and 
 
WHEREAS, the Town Board has not identified any other involved agencies for  
the proposed action, as such SEQRA regulations state that in cases in which there is  
only one involved agency, in this case the Riverhead Town Board, coordinated review is 
not required and said agency must assume the responsibilities of Lead Agency. Now,  
therefore, be it 
 
RESOLVED, the Town Clerk is hereby authorized to publish the attached public notice to 
consider a local law to amend Chapter 301 Zoning and Land Development, Part 3 Supplementary 
Use Regulations, Article LIIC Cannabis, § 301-283.20. Location and Number of Permitted Retail and 
On-Site Consumption and § 301-283.25 When Effective of the Riverhead Town Code once in the 
May 29, 2025 issue of the News-Review Newspaper, the newspaper hereby designated as the 
official newspaper for this purpose, and also to cause a copy of the proposed amendment to be 
posted on the sign board of the Town; and be it further 
 
 RESOLVED, that the Town Clerk be and is hereby directed to forward a copy of 
this resolution to Planning Department and the Office of the Town Attorney; and be it 
further 
  
RESOLVED, that all Town Hall Departments may review and obtain a copy of 
this resolution from the electronic storage device and, if needed, a certified copy of 
same may be obtained from the Office of the Town Clerk.    
 
THE VOTE

Chapter 301 Zoning and Land Development 
Part 3 Supplementary Regulations 
Article LIIC Cannabis 
 
§ 301-283.20. Location and number of permitted retail and on-site consumption 
establishments. 
The location and maximum number of each type of establishment permitted in the Town of 
Riverhead is governed by the subsections below. 
A. Location requirements. Cannabis retail and on -site consumption establishments shall be 
permitted in only the Business Center; Shopping Center; Destination Retail Center; 
Downtown Center 1; Downtown Center 2; Downtown Center 3;  Hamlet Center; Rural 
Corridor; Village Center; Business CR; Peconic River Community; and Business F Zoning 
Districts subject to the following requirements: 
(1) No retail or on -site consumption establishment shall be established or located within 
1,000 feet, measured from the nearest property lines of each of the affected parcels, of 
any school, library or day-care facility. 
(2) No retail or on-site consumption establishment shall be established or located within 500 
feet, measured from the nearest property lines of each of the affected parcels, of any Town 
beach, playground or community center, and children's amusement. 
(3) No retail or on-site consumption establishment shall be established or located within 500 
feet, measured using a straight line from the center of the nearest entrance of the place 
of worship to the center of the establishment, of any place of worship. 
(4) No retail or on -site consumption establishment shall be established or located within 
2,500 feet, measured from the nearest property lines of each of the affected parcels, of 
any other cannabis retail or on -site consumption establishment. Notwithstanding t he 
above, only one cannabis retail or on-site consumption establishment shall be permitted 
in Commercial Corridors One, Two, Four and Five.  
(5) No retail or on -site consumption establishment shall be established or located within 
1,000 feet, measured from the nearest property lines of each of the affected parcels, of 
any existing residential use, except those properties with frontage along and located 
within Commercial Corridors One, Two, Three, Four and Five. 
(6) No retail or on-site consumption establishment shall be established or located within a 
mixed-use development project containing a residential use component. 
B. Retailers shall be required to comply with all zoning, land use, and development regulations 
applicable to the underlying zoning district in which they are permitted to establish and 
operate as set forth in the Town Code for the Town of Riverhead. 
C. Prior to applying for any building permit, use permit, special permit or site plan, or any other 
applicable land use application the applicant or their representative shall cause to be filed a 
“Notification to Municipality” also known as OCM -06009 in the Office of the Town Clerk. 
Pursuant to the MRTA the Town shall have thirty (30) days to express and opinion regarding 
the proposed location to the Cannabis Control Board, with the Town reserving the right to 
10.42.a
Packet Pg. 187
Attachment: 2025-05-02_Amends 301-283.20 Location and number of permitted retail and on-site consumption establsihments(Cannabis) & 301-
 
 
request a one-time 30-day extension of time for generating said Opinion Letter. An Opinion 
Letter recommending approval with a determination that the application and its proposed site 
location meets and complies with Town Code (Article LIIC “Cannabis”) to the Cannabis 
Control Board shall be valid for a period not to exceed ninety  (90) days from the date of 
issuance. 
D. Within ninety (90) days of issuance of the Town’s Opinion Letter recommending approval 
with a determination that the application and its proposed site location meets and complies 
with Town Code (Article LIIC “Cannabis”) to the Cannabis Control Board, the applicant shall 
file or caused to be filed a copy of the cannabis license for the location set forth in the Opinion 
Letter, together with an application and submission of all requisite fees for any building 
permit, use permit, special permit or site plan, o r any other applicable land use application 
required pursuant to Town Code. Applicant’s failure to file the relevant land use application 
as described herein above within the ninety (90) day period, shall be deemed an abandonment 
of its application to loca te within the Town of Riverhead and said Opinion Letter shall no 
longer be valid. In the event the applicant has complied with the filing requirements within 
the ninety (90) days, then the application shall be extended for such period of time for 
approval or denial of such building permit, use permit, special permit or site plan or any other 
relevant land use application. 
E. Notwithstanding the above, upon expiration of the time parameters set forth in ( C) and (D) 
above, Applicant may submit a new Notification to Municipality for the proposed location  
under the identical terms and conditions set forth herein. 
 
§ 301-283.25 A. When effective. Statutory Authority 
This article shall take effect immediately upon filing with the Secretary of State. is enacted pursuant 
to the provisions of Article 6, Section 131(2) of the MRTA and the Municipal Home Rule Laws of 
the State of New York. 
 
§ 301-283.25 B. Severability. 
In the event that any section of this chapter be decided by the courts to be unconstitutional or 
invalid in whole or in part, such decision shall not affect the validity of this chapter as a whole or 
any part thereof other than that so decided to be unconstitutional or invalid. 
 
§ 301-283.25 C. When Effective. 
This article shall take effect immediately upon filing with the Secretary of State.

Part 1 - Project and Setting 
Instructions for Completing Part 1 
Part 1 is to be completed by the applicant or project sponsor.  Responses become part of the application for approval or funding, 
are subject to public review, and may be subject to further verification. 
Complete Part 1 based on information currently available.  If additional research or investigation would be needed to fully respond to 
any item, please answer as thoroughly as possible based on current information; indicate whether missing information does not exist, 
or is not reasonably available to the sponsor; and, when possible, generally describe work or studies which would be necessary to 
update or fully develop that information. 
Applicants/sponsors must complete all items in Sections A & B.  In Sections C, D & E, most items contain an initial question that 
must be answered either “Yes” or “No”. If the answer to the initial question is “Yes”, complete the sub-questions that follow.  If the 
answer to the initial question is “No”, proceed to the next question. Section F allows the project sponsor to identify and attach any 
additional information.  Section G requires the name and signature of the applicant or project sponsor to verify that the information 
contained in Part 1is accurate and complete.

TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
 
TB Resolution 2025-463 
 
AUTHORIZE TOWN CLERK TO PUBLISH AND POST PUBLIC NOTICE TO 
CONSIDER A LOCAL LAW TO AMEND CHAPTER 217 OF THE RIVERHEAD TOWN 
CODE TITLED “BUILDINGS, BUILDING CONSTRUCTION AND IMPROVEMENTS 
AND HOUSING STANDARDS”, SECTION 8 THEREOF TITLED, “DEMOLITION

TOWN OF RIVERHEAD  
NOTICE OF PUBLIC HEARING  
 
 PLEASE TAKE NOTICE that a public hearing will be held before the Town Board of the 
Town of Riverhead at Riverhead Town Hall, 4 West Second Street, Riverhead, New York, on the 
1st day of July, 2025 at or about 2:15 p.m. to amend “Buildings, Building Construction and 
Improvements and Housing Standards”, Section 8 thereof titled, “Demolition permits”. 
 
The intent of the proposed legislation is to distinguish between ordinary demolition 
permits and demolition permits required for code violations, include timelines for both and add 
that electrical or gas service disconnects may be required. 
 
 A copy of the entire text of the proposed local law and the provisions of the existing law to 
be amended may be reviewed at the Office of the Town Clerk, 4 West Second Street, Riverhead, 
New York 11901, between the hours of 8:30 a.m. and 4:30 p.m., Monday through Friday and can 
be accessed on the Town of Riverhead website at: www.townofriverheadny.gov under the Agenda 
and Minutes for the May 21, 2025 Town Board Meeting. 
Dated:  Riverhead, New York 
  May 21, 2025 
 
 
 BY THE ORDER OF THE TOWN BOARD 
 OF THE TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
 JAMES M. WOOTEN, Town Clerk 
 
10.43.a
Packet Pg. 205
Attachment: Notice of Public Hearing 217.8 Demo Permits  (2025-463 : Publish and Post Public Notice to Amend 217.8 Demolition Permits)
Chapter 217. Buildings, Building Construction and 
Improvements and Housing Standards 
Part 1. Administration and Enforcement of Uniform Code 
Article I. Administration and Enforcement 
§ 217-8. Demolition permits, Ordinary, Violation Based. 
 
A. Demolition permits shall be applied for the same as building permits, but with no plans needed 
unless specified by the Building Inspector. However, In addition, specifications and diagrams 
showing methods to be used for needling or shoring adjacent buildings  and electrical or gas 
service disconnects may be required by the Building Inspector. Ordinary demolition permits 
shall be non-renewable unless approved by the Building Inspector and all specified work shall 
be commenced within forty-five (45) days of issuance and completed within one (1) year of the 
date of issuance. 
 
B. Demolition permits issued pursuant to the remediation of any violation of this code or any state 
code shall be non -renewable and work shall be commenced within forty -five (45) days of 
issuance and completed within six (6) months of the date of issuance.

TOWN OF RIVERHEAD  
NOTICE OF PUBLIC HEARING  
 
 PLEASE TAKE NOTICE that a public hearing will be held before the Town Board of the 
Town of Riverhead at Riverhead Town Hall, 4 West Second Street, Riverhead, New York, on the 
1st day of July, 2025 at or about 2:10 p.m. to amend Chapter 269 of the Riverhead Town 
Code titled “Shopping Carts”. 
 
The intent of the proposed legislation is to provide a definition for and require retail 
establishments to equip all shopping carts with an acceptable anti-theft wheel braking 
mechanism system.  
 
 A copy of the entire text of the proposed local law and the provisions of the existing law to 
be amended may be reviewed at the Office of the Town Clerk, 4 West Second Street, Riverhead, 
New York 11901, between the hours of 8:30 a.m. and 4:30 p.m., Monday through Friday and can 
be accessed on the Town of Riverhead website at: www.townofriverheadny.gov under the Agenda 
and Minutes for the May 21, 2025 Town Board Meeting. 
Dated:  Riverhead, New York 
  May 21, 2025 
 
 
 BY THE ORDER OF THE TOWN BOARD 
 OF THE TOWN OF RIVERHEAD 
 JAMES M. WOOTEN, Town Clerk 
 
10.44.a
Packet Pg. 209
Attachment: Notice of Public Hearing 269 Shopping Carts  (Anti-Theft Wheel Braking Mechanisms)  (2025-464 : Authorize Town Clerk to Publish
Chapter 269. Shopping Carts 
§ 269-2. Definitions; word usage. 
A. Definitions. When used in this chapter, the following terms shall have the meanings indicated: 
Acceptable Anti-Theft Wheel Braking Mechanisms System(s) 
1. Electromagnetic Wheel Locking: This system uses electromagnetic technology embedded in the wheels to lock 
them when the cart moves outside a designated area. The cart will stop moving or the wheels will lock if the cart 
crosses a defined boundary (like a parking lot line).  
2. Radio Frequency Identification (RFID) Based Systems: These systems use a combination of RFID tags on the 
carts and sensors placed around the store perimeter. If a cart with an active RFID tag goes past a sensor, the 
system will activate a brake or lock on the wheels to prevent further movement.  
3. Smart Cart System: GPS Tracking and Alerts: Shopping Carts equipped with GPS technology that can track the 
cart's movement. If the cart is moved outside of the designated area, store management is notified, and the 
wheels may be locked remotely. 
§ 269-6. Security devices. 
Any new application submitted to any Town department or board for the construction or conversion of any retail 
establishment located on Route 58, Route 25 and/or Route 25A shall require, as a condition of the approval of the 
application, that each shopping cart provided by the establishment be equipped with an anti-theft wheel braking 
mechanism or any other theft protection system. All current retail establishments located on Route 58, Route 25 
and/or Route 25A shall, within three months of the adoption of this Chapter 269, equip the shopping carts provided 
for on-site customer use with the security device system required by this chapter. 
A. Any new application submitted to any Town department or board for the construction or conversion of a 
retail establishment located on Route 58, Route 25, and/or Route 25A shall require, as a condition of the 
approval of the application, that the establishment complies with the requirements of this chapter, 
including equipping all shopping carts intended for customer use with an acceptable anti-theft wheel 
braking mechanism system as defined in this chapter.   
B. All pre-existing retail establishments located on Route 58, Route 25, and/or Route 25A must comply 
with the requirements of this section and equip all shopping carts intended for customer use with an 
acceptable anti-theft wheel braking mechanism system as defined in this chapter. 
Excepted from the foregoing requirements for anti-theft wheel braking mechanism systems are retail 
establishments that maintain or store fifteen (15) or fewer shopping carts on their premises at any time, 
however, any retail establishment storing fifteen (15) or fewer carts shall remove such carts from the parking 
areas before close of business each day.  
Underline represents addition(s) 
Strikethrough represents deletion(s)

License Agreement For Concession at South Jamesport Beach 
Between the Town of Riverhead and Antoine Maaiki 
 
This Agreement ("agreement"), made this ____________ day of May, 2025, between the Town of 
Riverhead, a Municipal Corporation of the State of New York, ("licensor") and Antoine Maaiki, 
an individual residing at 119 Sunrise Ave, Riverhead, New York, ("licensee"). 
 
W I T N E S S : 
 
Licensor owns and maintains park property described as South Jamesport Beach  located 
along Peconic Bay for the benefit of any use by Town residents and including a playground, beach 
volleyball areas, beach front, swimming, etc.  The Town also maintains a concession stand at the 
beach; and 
 
Licensee desires to obtain from licensor a license to operate a concession with certain 
privileges and rights in the concession stand located at South Jamesport Beach hereinafter referred 
to as “SJPB Concession Stand”; and 
 
The licensor deems it advantageous to itself, residents and to business entities located in 
the Town of Riverhead to grant to the licensee a license to operate a concession area with the rights 
and privileges as here set forth; and 
 
NOW, THEREFORE, in consideration of the premises and the mutual promises 
contained herein, the parties do hereby agree as follows: 
 
Article I. 
Licensed Premises 
 
Licensor, in consideration of the conditions, covenants and agreements set forth herein to be kept 
and performed by Licensee, for the purposes set forth herein does grant to Licensee use of the 
SJPB Concession Stand (sometimes referred to herein as the "licensed premises" or "premises"), 
all of which Licensee accepts, for the purposes set forth herein.  
 
Article II. 
Concession 
Use and Occupancy 
 
Licensee shall have the right to operate a concession at the SJPB Concession Stand  and in 
connection therewith the Licensee shall have the right to and shall sell items subject to the prior 
approval of the Town of Riverhead and to the limitations set forth below.  
 
 
 
10.46.a
Packet Pg. 216
Attachment: License Agreement - SJPB Concession Stand with Maaiki - 2025  (2025-466 : Authorize Supervisor to Execute License Agreement
 
 
A.  Merchandise: 
 
(1) Licensee shall be permitted to and shall sell on a non exclusive basis in the SJPB Concession 
Stand, the items listed below:  
 
Sandwiches, Salads, Hot Dogs, Nachos with Cheese , Hot Pretzels, Charcuterie Boards, Shrimp 
Cocktail, Assorted Platters, Snacks, Chips, Ice Cream, Candy, Water, Sports Drinks, Soda.  
 
(2) Except with prior written approval of the Town Board, the Licensee shall not install or operate 
any machines or devices of any nature, kind or type; nor shall he/she engage in any activities or 
sell any items other than those enumerated in the Initial Schedule of Merchandise or such other 
approved/amended Schedule of Merchandise. 
 
B.  Schedule of Operation: 
 
Licensee shall operate the concession on the following dates/times: Thursday through Sunday from 
Memorial Day weekend until the 4th of July weekend. Thereafter , beginning July 7, 2025 seven 
(7) days a week until the Labor Day weekend. Regular hours of operation shall be 8:00 AM – 4:00 
PM, but may extend to accommodate and be available to activities in the area, i.e., pickleball 
players, boaters returning to the East Creek Marina. In no event, however, shall the concession 
stand be open after 9:00 PM or before 7:00 AM. The failure to operate as required, unless for 
extraordinary circumstances, shall be deemed a failure to perform under the terms of this license 
agreement and may result in termination of the agreement, at the sole discretion of the Town. 
 
C.  Permits/Licenses. Licensee agrees to use and occupy the premises pursuant to all rules and 
regulations prescribed by the Town, and, to the extent applicable, all federal, state, county and 
town statutes, local laws, ordinances, rules, and regulations in existence during the periods 
covered by the license. In addition, Licensee shall obtain all required licenses and/or permits 
required by law to operate such concession. 
 
D.  The Licensee shall not assign, transfer, mortgage, or otherwise dispose of or encumber this 
license or any rights without the prior written consent of the Town. Any such attempt without 
consent of the Town shall be an automatic revocation and terminati on of this license , any 
improvements made to the SJPB Concession Stand or surrounding property shall be forfeited to 
the Town as liquidated damages. 
 
E.  The Licensee and the Town agree that nothing contained in this agreement is intended, or shall 
be construed as, creating or establishing a partnership or joint venture between the parties herein 
or as designating the Licensee as the agent or representa tive of the Town for any purpose 
whatsoever. 
 
F.  Licensee acknowledges and agrees that this License Agreement is subject to and subordinate 
to any existing or future agreement of any kind between the Town and any other agency of the

federal, state, any county, now or hereafter created, whether specifically mentioned herein or not, 
pertaining to the development, construction, operation or maintenance of SJPB Concession Stand, 
its walkways, playground and any such other improvements existing at SJPB Concession Stand. 
The Town reserves the right to further develop, improve, maintain, modify and repair the SJPB 
Concession Stand , walkways, playground and make any such other improvements at SJPB 
Concession Stand, at any time without interference or hindrance by the Licensee. The Town also

G.  The Licensee, at its own expense, shall keep the premises in good repair and agrees to surrender

as at the beginning of the term, ordinary wear and use being excepted, and shall pay for all damages 
occasioned by its use. 
 
H.  The Licensee shall recognize that the SJPB Concession Stand  and the surrounding property 
known as SJPB Concession Stand  is Town-owned property, thus, the Licensee shall not use the 
SJPB Concession Stand or  permit use of same by his employees or other authorized personnel, 
for any political purpose whatsoever. 
 
Article III 
Term 
 
The term of this Agreement shall be seasonal, commencing on May 22, 2025 and shall terminate 
on September 1, 2025.  
 
 
In the event Licensee shall, with the consent of the Licensor, hold over and remain in possession 
of the premises after the expiration of the term of this Agreement, such holding over shall not be 
deemed to operate as a renewal or extension of this Agreement, but shall only create an occupancy 
from month -to-month on the same terms, conditions, and covenants, including consideration, 
herein contained. 
 
Article IV. 
Rent 
 
Licensee accepts the subject premises in an “as is” condition. It is agreed that Lessee shall  pay a 
monthly license fee of $300.00 with the first payment due upon signing and the first day of each 
month thereafter until termination of license.  
 
A.  Licens or shall ensure that water source, electricity and such lighting fixtures necessary for 
operation of the concession stand are available in good working order, and Licensor shall apply 
paint to the interior of the concession stand.

B. In consideration of the monthly license fee set forth herein, Licensee shall install refrigeration

not limited to Suffolk County Health Department.  
 
C. Licensee shall not erect, install, operate nor cause or permit to be erected, installed or operated 
in or upon the granted premises any signs or other similar advertising device without first having 
obtained the written consent of the Chief Engineer for  the Town of Riverhead and Building 
Inspector for the Town of Riverhead.  
 
D. Licensee shall at all times throughout the term of the license maintain the improvements 
(including those installed by Licensee) and all other portions of the granted premises in good and 
serviceable condition and repair. In consideration of the monthly license fee set forth herein, 
Licensee shall paint the exterior of the structure and design and post a mural, the design of which 
must be given written approval by the Licensor.  
 
E.  Licensee shall keep the granted premises and the improvements free and clear of any and all 
liens in any way arising out of the action, or use by Licensee; provided, however, that Licensee 
may in good faith contest the validity of any lien sought to be imposed provided Licensee provides 
Licensor with such bonds or security that may be reasonably requested by Licensor. 
 
             Article V 
     Utility and Garbage Services 
 
A. Utility Service 
 
(1)  The Licensor shall provide basic utility services including electric, water, *sewer (if 
applicable), and light required for or in connection with the operation and maintenance of the 
licensed premises.  
 
(2)  Any upgrade of the services, i.e. installation of equipment required for preparation of food or 
cold storage of food shall require approval of the Town and Licensee shall bear the sole expense. 
Any permits necessary from any state or local governmenta l agencies for an upgrade to services 
shall be the responsibility of the Licensee and Licensee shall be solely responsible for the costs or 
charges over and above the basic utility services provided by Licensor.   
 
(3)  Licensor will in no event be liable for any interruption or failure of utility services on the 
premises. 
 
B. Garbage Service 
 
(1)  The Licensor agrees to provide garbage service to the premises.
